<p>During the <a href="/wiki/2016_Republican_National_Convention" title="2016 Republican National Convention">Republican National Convention</a>, Carson appeared with former New York City Mayor <a href="/wiki/Rudy_Giuliani" title="Rudy Giuliani">Rudy Giuliani</a> in support of the pro-Donald Trump <a href="/wiki/Great_America_PAC" title="Great America PAC">Great America PAC</a> at an event in Cleveland.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178"><a href="#cite_note-178">[178]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Trump_administration_role_and_selection_as_nominee_for_HUD_Secretary">Trump administration role and selection as nominee for HUD Secretary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ben_Carson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Trump administration role and selection as nominee for HUD Secretary">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>After Donald Trump's win in the 2016 election, Ben Carson joined <a href="/wiki/Presidential_transition_of_Donald_Trump" title="Presidential transition of Donald Trump">Trump's transition team</a> as Vice Chairman. Carson was also offered a cabinet position in the administration. He declined, in part because of his lack of experience, with an aide stating, "The last thing he would want to do was take a position that could cripple the presidency."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hill_179-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hill-179">[179]</a></sup> Although it was reported that the position was for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Secretary_of_Health_and_Human_Services" title="Secretary of Health and Human Services">Secretary of Health and Human Services</a>, Carson's business manager has disputed this, stating, "Dr. Carson was never offered a specific position, but everything was open to him."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hill_179-1"><a href="#cite_note-Hill-179">[179]</a></sup> He was eventually offered the position of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Secretary_of_Housing_and_Urban_Development" title="Secretary of Housing and Urban Development">Secretary of Housing and Urban Development</a>, which he accepted.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-180"><a href="#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup></p>
<p>On December 5, 2016, President-elect Donald Trump announced that he would nominate Carson to the position of Secretary of Housing and Urban Development.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-181"><a href="#cite_note-181">[181]</a></sup> During confirmation hearings, Carson was held under close scrutiny for his lack of experience. On January 24, 2017, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Senate_Banking_Committee" title="Senate Banking Committee">Senate Banking Committee</a>, including Democratic Senators <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_Warren" title="Elizabeth Warren">Elizabeth Warren</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sherrod_Brown" title="Sherrod Brown">Sherrod Brown</a>, voted unanimously to approve the nomination, sending it to the Senate floor for a complete vote.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182">[182]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Carson_Scholars_Fund">Carson Scholars Fund</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ben_Carson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Carson Scholars Fund">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>In 1994, Carson and his wife started the Carson Scholars Fund, which awards scholarships to students in grades 4–11 for "academic excellence and humanitarian qualities".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CSF_183-0"><a href="#cite_note-CSF-183">[183]</a></sup> They founded it after reading that U.S. students ranked second to last in terms of math and science testing among 22 countries. They also noticed that schools awarded athletes with trophies, whereas honor students only received "a pin or certificate."</p>
<p>Recipients of the Carson Scholars Fund receive a $1,000 scholarship towards their college education. It has awarded 6,700 scholarships.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CSF_183-1"><a href="#cite_note-CSF-183">[183]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184">[184]</a></sup> In recognition for his work with the Carson Scholars Fund and other charitable giving throughout his lifetime, Carson was awarded the <a href="/wiki/William_E._Simon_Prize_for_Philanthropic_Leadership" title="William E. Simon Prize for Philanthropic Leadership">William E. Simon Prize for Philanthropic Leadership</a> in 2005.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185"><a href="#cite_note-185">[185]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ben_Carson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Personal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Carson and his wife, <a href="/wiki/Candy_Carson" title="Candy Carson">Lacena "Candy" Rustin</a>, met in 1971 as students at <a href="/wiki/Yale_University" title="Yale University">Yale University</a>. They married in 1975 and lived in <a href="/wiki/Howard_County,_Maryland" title="Howard County, Maryland">Howard County, Maryland</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186"><a href="#cite_note-186">[186]</a></sup> before moving in 2001 to <a href="/wiki/West_Friendship,_Maryland" title="West Friendship, Maryland">West Friendship, Maryland</a>, where they had purchased a 48-acre property.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_187-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0-187">[187]</a></sup> Together, the couple have three sons (Rhoeyce, Benjamin Jr., and Murray), as well as several grandchildren. Their youngest son, Murray, was born in <a href="/wiki/Perth" title="Perth">Perth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a>, while Carson was undertaking a residency there.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-perth_93-1"><a href="#cite_note-perth-93">[93]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2013, Carson, his wife, and Carson's mother moved to <a href="/wiki/West_Palm_Beach,_Florida" title="West Palm Beach, Florida">West Palm Beach, Florida</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188"><a href="#cite_note-188">[188]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-189"><a href="#cite_note-189">[189]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ben_Carson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ben_Carson_by_Gage_Skidmore_10.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3744" data-file-width="5616" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Ben_Carson_by_Gage_Skidmore_10.jpg/220px-Ben_Carson_by_Gage_Skidmore_10.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Ben_Carson_by_Gage_Skidmore_10.jpg/330px-Ben_Carson_by_Gage_Skidmore_10.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Ben_Carson_by_Gage_Skidmore_10.jpg/440px-Ben_Carson_by_Gage_Skidmore_10.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ben_Carson_by_Gage_Skidmore_10.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Carson speaking at a church service in Des Moines, Iowa</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Carson and his wife are members of the <a href="/wiki/Seventh-day_Adventist_Church" title="Seventh-day Adventist Church">Seventh-day Adventist Church</a> (SDA).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-notable_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-notable-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-redland_baptist_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-redland_baptist-4">[4]</a></sup> Carson was baptized at Burns Seventh-day Adventist Church on Detroit's eastside. A few years later, he told the pastor at a church he was attending in <a href="/wiki/Inkster,_Michigan" title="Inkster, Michigan">Inkster, Michigan</a> that he had not fully understood his first baptism and wanted to be baptized again, so he was.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-190"><a href="#cite_note-190">[190]</a></sup> He has served as a local elder and <a href="/wiki/Sabbath_School" title="Sabbath School">Sabbath School</a> teacher in the Seventh-day Adventist Church.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191"><a href="#cite_note-191">[191]</a></sup> His mother is a devout Seventh-day Adventist.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-192"><a href="#cite_note-192">[192]</a></sup> Although Carson is an Adventist, the church has officially cautioned church employees to remain politically neutral.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SDA_caution_193-0"><a href="#cite_note-SDA_caution-193">[193]</a></sup></p>
<p>In keeping with his Seventh-day Adventist faith Carson announced in 2014 his belief, "that the United States will play a big role" in the coming apocalypse. He went on to say, "I hope by that time I'm not around anymore."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-194"><a href="#cite_note-194">[194]</a></sup></p>
<p>In an interview with <a href="/wiki/Katie_Couric" title="Katie Couric">Katie Couric</a>, Carson said that Jesus Christ came to Earth to redeem the world through His atoning sacrifice and that all people are sinners and need His redemption.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-195"><a href="#cite_note-195">[195]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-196"><a href="#cite_note-196">[196]</a></sup></p>
<p>Carson has stated he does not believe in hell as understood by some Christians: "You know, I see God as a very loving individual. And why would he torment somebody forever who only had a life of 60 or 70 or 80 years? Even if they were evil. Even if they were only evil for 80 years?". This is fully in line with Adventist teaching, which promotes <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Annihiliationism" title="Annihiliationism">annihiliationism</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-annih_197-0"><a href="#cite_note-annih-197">[197]</a></sup></p>
<p>Carson endorsed <a href="/wiki/Seventh-day_Adventist_theology" title="Seventh-day Adventist theology">Seventh-day Adventist theology</a>, which includes belief in a <a href="/wiki/Biblical_literalism" title="Biblical literalism">literal reading</a> of the first chapters of <a href="/wiki/Book_of_Genesis" title="Book of Genesis">Genesis</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KraussNewYorker_198-0"><a href="#cite_note-KraussNewYorker-198">[198]</a></sup> In a 2013 interview with <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Adventist_News_Network" title="Adventist News Network">Adventist News Network</a></i>, Carson said "You know, I’m proud of the fact that I believe what God has said, and I’ve said many times that I’ll defend it before anyone. If they want to criticize the fact that I believe in a literal, six-day creation, let's have at it because I will poke all kinds of holes in what they believe."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ANN_chat_199-0"><a href="#cite_note-ANN_chat-199">[199]</a></sup> Carson's Adventism was raised as an issue by his then-primary rival <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">Donald Trump</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-trumpsda_200-0"><a href="#cite_note-trumpsda-200">[200]</a></sup> Some Adventists have argued that Carson's political positions on <a href="/wiki/Gun_rights" title="Gun rights">gun rights</a> and <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_religion" title="Freedom of religion">religious liberty</a> conflict with historic Adventist teachings in favor of nonviolence, pacifism, and the <a href="/wiki/Separation_of_church_and_state" title="Separation of church and state">separation of church and state</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SDA_caution_193-1"><a href="#cite_note-SDA_caution-193">[193]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gunadventist_201-0"><a href="#cite_note-gunadventist-201">[201]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Vegetarianism">Vegetarianism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ben_Carson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Vegetarianism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Consistent with the practice of many Adventists, Carson is a lacto-ovo <a href="/wiki/Vegetarianism" title="Vegetarianism">vegetarian</a> (he will eat dishes containing milk, eggs, or cheese, and occasionally, poultry).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hopkinson2015_202-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hopkinson2015-202">[202]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kim1990_203-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kim1990-203">[203]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carson1999_204-0"><a href="#cite_note-Carson1999-204">[204]</a></sup> He has said his main reason for becoming vegetarian was health concerns, including avoiding parasites and heart disease, and he emphasizes the <a href="/wiki/Environmental_vegetarianism" title="Environmental vegetarianism">environmental benefits of vegetarianism</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kim1990_203-1"><a href="#cite_note-Kim1990-203">[203]</a></sup> His transition was made easier because he had eaten little meat for aesthetic reasons as a child,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kim1990_203-2"><a href="#cite_note-Kim1990-203">[203]</a></sup> and he readily adopted his wife's vegetarianism because she does much of the cooking in their household.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kim1990_203-3"><a href="#cite_note-Kim1990-203">[203]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carson1999_204-1"><a href="#cite_note-Carson1999-204">[204]</a></sup> Speaking in 1990, he said that with the increasing availability of meat substitutes, "It might take 20 years. But eventually there will no longer be a reason for most people to eat meat. And animals will breathe a sigh of relief."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kim1990_203-4"><a href="#cite_note-Kim1990-203">[203]</a></sup> To avoid causing others discomfort, he is willing to occasionally eat chicken or turkey, although he finds eating pork highly unpleasant.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carson1999_204-2"><a href="#cite_note-Carson1999-204">[204]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_and_related_positions">Political and related positions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ben_Carson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Political and related positions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dr._Ben_Carson_in_New_Hampshire_on_August_13th,_2015_1_by_Michael_Vadon_30.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4320" data-file-width="6480" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Dr._Ben_Carson_in_New_Hampshire_on_August_13th%2C_2015_1_by_Michael_Vadon_30.jpg/220px-Dr._Ben_Carson_in_New_Hampshire_on_August_13th%2C_2015_1_by_Michael_Vadon_30.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Dr._Ben_Carson_in_New_Hampshire_on_August_13th%2C_2015_1_by_Michael_Vadon_30.jpg/330px-Dr._Ben_Carson_in_New_Hampshire_on_August_13th%2C_2015_1_by_Michael_Vadon_30.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Dr._Ben_Carson_in_New_Hampshire_on_August_13th%2C_2015_1_by_Michael_Vadon_30.jpg/440px-Dr._Ben_Carson_in_New_Hampshire_on_August_13th%2C_2015_1_by_Michael_Vadon_30.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dr._Ben_Carson_in_New_Hampshire_on_August_13th,_2015_1_by_Michael_Vadon_30.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Carson in <a href="/wiki/New_Hampshire" title="New Hampshire">New Hampshire</a>, August 13, 2015</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Abortion_and_human_fetal_tissue">Abortion and human fetal tissue</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ben_Carson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Abortion and human fetal tissue">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Carson has described himself as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pro-life" title="Pro-life">pro-life</a>, comparing women who have abortions to historical slave owners,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-205"><a href="#cite_note-205">[205]</a></sup> and supports overturning the 1973 Supreme Court decision in <i><a href="/wiki/Roe_v._Wade" title="Roe v. Wade">Roe v. Wade</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RVW_206-0"><a href="#cite_note-RVW-206">[206]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MTP_NYT_207-0"><a href="#cite_note-MTP_NYT-207">[207]</a></sup> He opposes access to abortion in virtually all cases, including pregnancies resulting from incest or rape,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RVW_206-1"><a href="#cite_note-RVW-206">[206]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MTP_NYT_207-1"><a href="#cite_note-MTP_NYT-207">[207]</a></sup> but would consider allowing its use if a woman's health is in danger.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RVW_206-2"><a href="#cite_note-RVW-206">[206]</a></sup> In August 2015, Carson said, "The number-one cause of death for black people is abortion."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNNLINES_208-0"><a href="#cite_note-CNNLINES-208">[208]</a></sup></p>
<p>After <a href="/wiki/Planned_Parenthood_2015_undercover_videos_controversy" title="Planned Parenthood 2015 undercover videos controversy">undercover videos</a> recorded by an anti-abortion group showed <a href="/wiki/Planned_Parenthood" title="Planned Parenthood">Planned Parenthood</a> officials discussing the donation of tissue from aborted fetuses for medical research,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-209"><a href="#cite_note-209">[209]</a></sup> Carson condemned the videos and argued that fetal tissue had no use in medical research, saying: "there's nothing that can't be done without fetal tissue."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-210"><a href="#cite_note-210">[210]</a></sup> Subsequently, Jen Gunter, an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Obstetrician-gynecologist" title="Obstetrician-gynecologist">obstetrician-gynecologist</a> and blogger – identified research that Carson himself had performed and published using tissue from fetuses aborted in the 9th and 17th weeks of gestation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jen_Gunter_211-0"><a href="#cite_note-Jen_Gunter-211">[211]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-212"><a href="#cite_note-212">[212]</a></sup> Carson defended his past use of tissue from aborted fetuses for medical research in part, by stating, "to not use the tissue that is in a tissue bank, regardless of where it comes from, would be foolish. Why would anybody not do that?"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-213"><a href="#cite_note-213">[213]</a></sup> Carson also told the <i>Washington Post</i>: "If you're killing babies and taking the tissue, that's a very different thing than taking a dead specimen and keeping a record of it."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-214"><a href="#cite_note-214">[214]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate_change">Climate change</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ben_Carson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Climate change">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Carson <a href="/wiki/Climate_change_denial" title="Climate change denial">rejects</a> the <a href="/wiki/Scientific_opinion_on_climate_change" title="Scientific opinion on climate change">scientific consensus that human activity causes climate change</a>; in November 2014, he said: "there's always going to be either cooling or warming going on", and he found the debate on climate change "irrelevant" and a distraction from protecting the environment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-215"><a href="#cite_note-215">[215]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2015, Carson expressed his disbelief about the scientific consensus on climate change, at a <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_Club_of_California" title="Commonwealth Club of California">Commonwealth Club</a> forum in San Francisco.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Monzon_216-0"><a href="#cite_note-Monzon-216">[216]</a></sup> After this statement, <a href="/wiki/Governor_of_California" title="Governor of California">Governor</a> <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Brown" title="Jerry Brown">Jerry Brown</a> of California sent Carson a flash drive containing the <a href="/wiki/Intergovernmental_Panel_on_Climate_Change" title="Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change">Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change</a>'s Synthesis Report, which details the scientific evidence of human impact on climate change.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Monzon_216-1"><a href="#cite_note-Monzon-216">[216]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Riotta_217-0"><a href="#cite_note-Riotta-217">[217]</a></sup> Carson's response to the <i><a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Chronicle" title="San Francisco Chronicle">San Francisco Chronicle</a></i> was: "There is no overwhelming science that the things that are going on are man-caused and not naturally caused."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Monzon_216-2"><a href="#cite_note-Monzon-216">[216]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Riotta_217-1"><a href="#cite_note-Riotta-217">[217]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Economic_issues">Economic issues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ben_Carson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Economic issues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Budget_and_Social_Security">Budget and Social Security</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ben_Carson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Budget and Social Security">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Carson blames Washington politicians for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_national_debt" title="United States national debt">national debt</a> and supports a <a href="/wiki/Balanced_budget_amendment" title="Balanced budget amendment">balanced budget amendment</a> to the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Constitution" title="United States Constitution">United States Constitution</a>, but has not explained how he would cut spending or raise revenue to achieve a balanced budget.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNN_Money_218-0"><a href="#cite_note-CNN_Money-218">[218]</a></sup> In May 2015, Carson said that "I don't think we should even talk about <a href="/wiki/Entitlement" title="Entitlement">entitlements</a> until we fix the economy, and I think fixing the economy is not going to be difficult."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNN_Money_218-1"><a href="#cite_note-CNN_Money-218">[218]</a></sup> Former head of the <a href="/wiki/Congressional_Budget_Office" title="Congressional Budget Office">Congressional Budget Office</a> <a href="/wiki/Douglas_Holtz-Eakin" title="Douglas Holtz-Eakin">Douglas Holtz-Eakin</a> criticized this statement, noting the U.S. debt is primarily "attributable to significant growth" in entitlement spending (i.e., <a href="/wiki/Social_Security_(United_States)" title="Social Security (United States)">Social Security</a> and <a href="/wiki/Medicare_(United_States)" title="Medicare (United States)">Medicare</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNN_Money_218-2"><a href="#cite_note-CNN_Money-218">[218]</a></sup></p>
<p>Carson proposed raising the minimum age to receive Social Security benefits to <a href="/wiki/Social_Security_debate_in_the_United_States" title="Social Security debate in the United States">extend the program's solvency</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto_219-0"><a href="#cite_note-auto-219">[219]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Taxation">Taxation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ben_Carson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Taxation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In August 2015, Carson proposed instituting a flat tax on personal and corporate income, and a <a href="/wiki/Capital_gains_tax" title="Capital gains tax">capital gains tax</a> of 10%; Carson claiming inspiration by the biblical concept of <a href="/wiki/Tithe" title="Tithe">tithing</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNN_Money_218-3"><a href="#cite_note-CNN_Money-218">[218]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-220"><a href="#cite_note-220">[220]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Citizens_for_Tax_Justice" title="Citizens for Tax Justice">Citizens for Tax Justice</a> found that this plan would "raise only 32 percent of the revenue of the current tax system and pay for only 28 percent of estimated government spending" and "would increase the deficit by $3 trillion in just one year," even with every tax deduction eliminated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PhillipsCTJ_221-0"><a href="#cite_note-PhillipsCTJ-221">[221]</a></sup></p>
<p>Carson referred to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Progressive_taxation" title="Progressive taxation">progressive taxation</a> as "socialism" in the first Republican primary debate,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-222"><a href="#cite_note-222">[222]</a></sup> proposing that the U.S. abandon its current <a href="/wiki/Income_tax_in_the_United_States" title="Income tax in the United States">graduated personal income tax</a> system in favor of a <a href="/wiki/Flat_tax" title="Flat tax">flat tax</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNN_Money_218-4"><a href="#cite_note-CNN_Money-218">[218]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-PhillipsCTJ_221-1"><a href="#cite_note-PhillipsCTJ-221">[221]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BelvedereTaxes_223-0"><a href="#cite_note-BelvedereTaxes-223">[223]</a></sup> Carson specifically proposed a 14.9% flat tax on both personal and business income, applying to income above 150 percent of the federal poverty level. Citizens whose income is at or below that level would be required to make an annual de minimis tax payment. Carson also proposed eliminating the capital gains tax, the <a href="/wiki/Alternative_minimum_tax" title="Alternative minimum tax">alternative minimum tax</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Estate_tax_in_the_United_States" title="Estate tax in the United States">estate tax</a>; and individual taxes on dividends and interest. The plan would do away with deductions and other tax breaks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-224"><a href="#cite_note-224">[224]</a></sup> Along with a flat tax, Carson has advocated for a national <a href="/wiki/Luxury_tax" title="Luxury tax">luxury tax</a> on "very expensive" goods.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BloombergEconomy_225-0"><a href="#cite_note-BloombergEconomy-225">[225]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-226"><a href="#cite_note-226">[226]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Steve_Forbes" title="Steve Forbes">Steve Forbes</a> preferred Carson's plan over those of the other Republican candidates.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-227"><a href="#cite_note-227">[227]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Financial_and_other_regulation">Financial and other regulation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ben_Carson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Financial and other regulation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Although most of Carson's economic policy beliefs reflected "current Republican orthodoxy," he diverged from other Republican presidential candidates in his support for reinstating <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Glass%E2%80%93Steagall_Legislation" title="Glass–Steagall Legislation">Glass-Steagall</a>, a <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Clutch_Plague&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Clutch Plague (page does not exist)">Depression</a>-era law that separated commercial and investment banks and was <a href="/wiki/Gramm%E2%80%93Leach%E2%80%93Bliley_Act" title="Gramm–Leach–Bliley Act">repealed in 1999</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BloombergEconomy_225-1"><a href="#cite_note-BloombergEconomy-225">[225]</a></sup> Carson believes the repeal of Glass-Steagall helped foster growth in banks that made them <a href="/wiki/Too_big_to_fail" title="Too big to fail">too big to fail</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BloombergEconomy_225-2"><a href="#cite_note-BloombergEconomy-225">[225]</a></sup></p>
<p>Carson was a critic of regulations more broadly, arguing that "every single regulation costs money" and hurts consumers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WaPo.cluelessness_228-0"><a href="#cite_note-WaPo.cluelessness-228">[228]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Minimum_wage_and_employment">Minimum wage and employment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ben_Carson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Minimum wage and employment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>During the 2016 presidential campaign, Carson initially said the current <a href="/wiki/Minimum_wage_in_the_United_States" title="Minimum wage in the United States">federal minimum wage</a> of $7.25 should "possibly" or "probably" be higher.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-229"><a href="#cite_note-229">[229]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ZillmanMinimumWage_230-0"><a href="#cite_note-ZillmanMinimumWage-230">[230]</a></sup> He supported a two-tiered minimum wage system, with a lower "starter" minimum wage for young workers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ZillmanMinimumWage_230-1"><a href="#cite_note-ZillmanMinimumWage-230">[230]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-231"><a href="#cite_note-231">[231]</a></sup> He also supported indexing the minimum wage to inflation, "so that we never have to have this conversation again in the history of America."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ZillmanMinimumWage_230-2"><a href="#cite_note-ZillmanMinimumWage-230">[230]</a></sup> At a Republican primary debate in November 2015, however, Carson argued against increasing the minimum wage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-The_POLITICO_Wrongometer_232-0"><a href="#cite_note-The_POLITICO_Wrongometer-232">[232]</a></sup></p>
<p>In October 2015, Carson called the size of the federal workforce "absurd" and called for reducing it by attrition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BelvedereTaxes_223-1"><a href="#cite_note-BelvedereTaxes-223">[223]</a></sup> In June 2015, Carson told a crowd of Republicans in Iowa that he was "thinking very seriously" about adding "a <a href="/wiki/Covert_operation" title="Covert operation">covert</a> division of people who look like the people in this room, who monitor what government people do."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-233"><a href="#cite_note-233">[233]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Trade_policy">Trade policy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ben_Carson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Trade policy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Carson praised the concept of <a href="/wiki/Free_trade" title="Free trade">free trade</a>, but voiced objections to the <a href="/wiki/Trans-Pacific_Partnership" title="Trans-Pacific Partnership">Trans-Pacific Partnership</a>, calling for the deal to be renegotiated, "because right now we have a lot of special interest groups who benefit."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BelvedereTaxes_223-2"><a href="#cite_note-BelvedereTaxes-223">[223]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-234"><a href="#cite_note-234">[234]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ben_Carson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In an October 2015 interview, Carson stated: "I actually have something I would use the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Education" title="United States Department of Education">Department of Education</a> to do. It would be to monitor our institutions of higher education for extreme political bias and deny federal funding on that basis."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carson_Blaze_235-0"><a href="#cite_note-Carson_Blaze-235">[235]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Soave_236-0"><a href="#cite_note-Soave-236">[236]</a></sup> This controversial suggestion was criticized by various commentators, who questioned its constitutionality and practicality.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Soave_236-1"><a href="#cite_note-Soave-236">[236]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MartinezProvocative_237-0"><a href="#cite_note-MartinezProvocative-237">[237]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-238"><a href="#cite_note-238">[238]</a></sup></p>
<p>Carson asserted that the <a href="/wiki/AP_United_States_History" title="AP United States History">AP U.S. History</a> overemphasizes wrongdoing (such as slavery, <a href="/wiki/Internment_of_Japanese_Americans" title="Internment of Japanese Americans">Japanese internment</a>, and atrocities against American Indians) by the United States, saying: "I think most people, when they finish that course, they'd be ready to go sign up for <a href="/wiki/Islamic_State_of_Iraq_and_the_Levant" title="Islamic State of Iraq and the Levant">ISIS</a>."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MartinezProvocative_237-1"><a href="#cite_note-MartinezProvocative-237">[237]</a></sup></p>
<p>In February 2015, at the annual Conservative Political Action Conference, Carson said: "I've found that homeschoolers do the best, private schoolers next best, charter schoolers next best, and public schoolers worst." On that basis, he advocated <a href="/wiki/School_choice" title="School choice">school choice</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-239"><a href="#cite_note-239">[239]</a></sup> Carson was a critic of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Common_Core_State_Standards" title="Common Core State Standards">Common Core State Standards</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-240"><a href="#cite_note-240">[240]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Evolution">Evolution</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ben_Carson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Evolution">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Carson's views on <a href="/wiki/Evolution" title="Evolution">evolution</a> and <a href="/wiki/Creationism" title="Creationism">creationism</a> have been controversial.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WPevolution_241-0"><a href="#cite_note-WPevolution-241">[241]</a></sup> In a 2006 debate, Carson stated: "I don't believe in evolution... I simply don't have enough faith to believe that something as complex as our ability to rationalize, think, and plan, and have a moral sense of what's right and wrong, just appeared."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-242"><a href="#cite_note-242">[242]</a></sup></p>
<p>In a 2011 speech to Seventh-day Adventists, entitled "Celebration of Creation", Carson said <a href="/wiki/Darwinism" title="Darwinism">Darwin's theory of evolution</a> "was encouraged by the adversary and it has become what is scientifically, politically correct"; with 'the adversary' being interpreted as a reference to <a href="/wiki/Satan" title="Satan">Satan</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-243"><a href="#cite_note-243">[243]</a></sup> Carson also labeled the theory of the <a href="/wiki/Big_Bang" title="Big Bang">Big Bang</a> as "ridiculous", saying, "Here you have all these <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/highfalutin#Adjective" title="wikt:highfalutin">highfalutin</a> scientists and they’re saying it was this gigantic explosion and everything came into perfect order ... I mean, you want to talk about fairy tales, that is amazing." Carson defended his comments in 2015, saying in regard to the scientific concepts, "I'm not going to denigrate you because of your faith and you shouldn't denigrate me for mine."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-244"><a href="#cite_note-244">[244]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-245"><a href="#cite_note-245">[245]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2014, Carson rejected the validity of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Carbon_dating" title="Carbon dating">carbon dating</a>, as it "really doesn't mean anything to a God who has the ability to create anything at any point in time". Carson further argued against evolution, stating his disbelief in the possibility of the "complexity of the human brain" arising "from a slime pit full of promiscuous biochemicals".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-246"><a href="#cite_note-246">[246]</a></sup></p>
<p>In October 2015, Carson stated that he does accept the idea of <a href="/wiki/Natural_selection" title="Natural selection">natural selection</a>, but there is only evidence for <a href="/wiki/Microevolution" title="Microevolution">microevolution</a> (changes in <a href="/wiki/Allele" title="Allele">allele</a> frequencies that occur over time <i>within</i> a species), which he believes was the result of "a wise creator who gave his creatures the ability to adapt to their environment so that he wouldn't have to start over every 50 years", whereas "there's never been one species that's turned into another species, that can be proved."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-David_247-0"><a href="#cite_note-David-247">[247]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Firearms_regulation_and_Nazi_Germany_comparisons">Firearms regulation and Nazi Germany comparisons</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ben_Carson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Firearms regulation and Nazi Germany comparisons">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Carson stated in 2013 that <a href="/wiki/Semi-automatic_firearm" title="Semi-automatic firearm">semi-automatic firearms</a> should be better regulated in large cities and high-crime areas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-248"><a href="#cite_note-248">[248]</a></sup> This statement attracted criticism from conservative opponents of gun control. Carson has declined to backtrack from that view, but says he is strongly in favor of the <a href="/wiki/Second_Amendment_to_the_United_States_Constitution" title="Second Amendment to the United States Constitution">Second Amendment</a>, and while guns being used on innocent people was "horrible" but "not nearly as horrible as having a population that is defenseless against a group of tyrants who have arms..."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-249"><a href="#cite_note-249">[249]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-250"><a href="#cite_note-250">[250]</a></sup> Carson made similar remarks in October 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CNNLINES_208-1"><a href="#cite_note-CNNLINES-208">[208]</a></sup> Carson stated on the campaign trail also said that if he were in a position of national authority, he would allow citizens to own any weapons, including automatic and semi-automatic guns, that they could legally buy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-251"><a href="#cite_note-251">[251]</a></sup></p>
<p>Carson has advanced the <a href="/wiki/Nazi_gun_control_theory" title="Nazi gun control theory">Nazi gun control theory</a>, asserting in his book, <i>A Perfect Union</i>, that <a href="/wiki/Gun_control" title="Gun control">gun control</a> made it easier for the Holocaust to occur: "Through a combination of removing guns and disseminating deceitful propaganda, the Nazis were able to carry out their evil intentions with relatively little resistance."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Basu_252-0"><a href="#cite_note-Basu-252">[252]</a></sup> In an interview with CNN's <a href="/wiki/Wolf_Blitzer" title="Wolf Blitzer">Wolf Blitzer</a>, Carson made similar claims.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Basu_252-1"><a href="#cite_note-Basu-252">[252]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Scott_253-0"><a href="#cite_note-Scott-253">[253]</a></sup> Holocaust historian <a href="/wiki/Alan_E._Steinweis" title="Alan E. Steinweis">Alan E. Steinweis</a> called Carson's stance "strangely ahistorical" because "no serious work of scholarship on the Nazi dictatorship or on the causes of the Holocaust" features "Nazi gun control measures...as a significant factor."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Steinweis_254-0"><a href="#cite_note-Steinweis-254">[254]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jonathan_Greenblatt" title="Jonathan Greenblatt">Jonathan Greenblatt</a>, national director and CEO of the <a href="/wiki/Anti-Defamation_League" title="Anti-Defamation League">Anti-Defamation League</a>, also criticized the remarks, calling them "mind-bending."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-255"><a href="#cite_note-255">[255]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Free_speech_and_Nazi_Germany_comparisons">Free speech and Nazi Germany comparisons</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ben_Carson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Free speech and Nazi Germany comparisons">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In March 2014, when asked about his previous claim that Americans were living "in a <a href="/wiki/Gestapo" title="Gestapo">Gestapo</a> age", Carson said that the United States is "very much like Nazi Germany ... [there] you had a government using its tools to intimidate a population." Carson stated that the "PC police" as well as politicians and the media "stifle people's conversation" and make them "afraid to say what they actually believe."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-256"><a href="#cite_note-256">[256]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-257"><a href="#cite_note-257">[257]</a></sup></p>
<p>In October 2015, Carson said he would "beg to differ" with people who thought America would never become something akin to <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi Germany</a>; stating: "If you go back and look at the history of the world, tyranny and despotism and how it starts, it has a lot to do with control of thought and control of speech." When questioned about whether he was comparing President Obama to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hitler" title="Hitler">Hitler</a>, Carson said: "No. I am saying in a situation where people do not express themselves, bad things can happen."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-258"><a href="#cite_note-258">[258]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the same month, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Washington_Post" title="The Washington Post">The Washington Post</a></i> called Carson "the biggest fan of Nazi metaphors in politics" in America, noting that Carson "doesn't shy away from holding up Nazi Germany as a dire warning of the slippery slope America is on" and had invoked Nazi Germany or Hitler in comments on various topics, including American society and "how a general population kept their mouth shut"; Obama supporters; socialists; gun rights; and <a href="/wiki/Planned_Parenthood" title="Planned Parenthood">Planned Parenthood</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-259"><a href="#cite_note-259">[259]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Healthcare">Healthcare</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ben_Carson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Healthcare">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Carson has been critical of the <a href="/wiki/Patient_Protection_and_Affordable_Care_Act" title="Patient Protection and Affordable Care Act">Patient Protection and Affordable Care Act</a>, saying in 2013 that "Obamacare is really I think the worst thing that has happened in this nation since slavery ... And it is in a way, it is slavery in a way, because it is making all of us subservient to the government, and it was never about health care. It was about control."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-260"><a href="#cite_note-260">[260]</a></sup> As an alternative to the Affordable Care Act, Carson said in 2013: "Here's my solution. When a person is born, give him a birth certificate, an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Electronic_medical_record" title="Electronic medical record">electronic medical record</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Health_savings_account" title="Health savings account">health savings account</a>."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-261"><a href="#cite_note-261">[261]</a></sup> In arguing that the Affordable Care Act gave the government "control of the people," Carson several times invoked a spurious quote from <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Lenin" title="Vladimir Lenin">Vladimir Lenin</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lenin_262-0"><a href="#cite_note-lenin-262">[262]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-heart-of-power_263-0"><a href="#cite_note-heart-of-power-263">[263]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Weiler_264-0"><a href="#cite_note-Weiler-264">[264]</a></sup></p>
<p>In a December 2014 op-ed for <i><a href="/wiki/The_Washington_Times" title="The Washington Times">The Washington Times</a></i>, Carson wrote: "we need to remove health care from the political arena and recognize that any government proposals affecting the health of all citizens should be free market-based and should be so appealing that it would not be necessary to force citizens into the program."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-265"><a href="#cite_note-265">[265]</a></sup></p>
<p>As a presidential candidate, Carson supported abolishing <a href="/wiki/Medicare_(United_States)" title="Medicare (United States)">Medicare</a> and <a href="/wiki/Medicaid" title="Medicaid">Medicaid</a>, moving dollars out of these "traditional health care" programs to fund new health savings accounts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CheneyMillman_266-0"><a href="#cite_note-CheneyMillman-266">[266]</a></sup> Carson proposed having the government contribute $2,000 to each individual's account annually, with individuals and employers permitted to contribute additional funds to the accounts, and unspent funds being allowed to be shared within a family.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CheneyMillman_266-1"><a href="#cite_note-CheneyMillman-266">[266]</a></sup> Carson has said that his plan "makes every family have their own <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Insurance_company" title="Insurance company">insurance company</a>."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CheneyMillman_266-2"><a href="#cite_note-CheneyMillman-266">[266]</a></sup> Carson estimated that his plan would cost the federal government $630 billion annually; this figure, however, does not account for population growth, <a href="/wiki/Inflation" title="Inflation">inflation</a>, or administrative costs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CheneyMillman_266-3"><a href="#cite_note-CheneyMillman-266">[266]</a></sup></p>
<p>Separately, Carson called in a 2014 op-ed for a system "similar to Medicare and Medicaid" for a group that Carson terms the "5 percent of patients with complex pre-existing or acquired maladies."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CheneyMillman_266-4"><a href="#cite_note-CheneyMillman-266">[266]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-267"><a href="#cite_note-267">[267]</a></sup> The cost of this system is not factored into Carson's $630 billion figure.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CheneyMillman_266-5"><a href="#cite_note-CheneyMillman-266">[266]</a></sup> In October 2015, Carson said if someone preferred the current Medicare or Medicaid programs to the health-savings-account approach, "I'm not going to deny you the privilege of doing that."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-268"><a href="#cite_note-268">[268]</a></sup></p>
<p>In a 1992 essay published in the <i>Harvard Journal of Minority Public Health</i>, Carson wrote that technological advancement will eventually lead to many people surviving their 100th birthdays, and questioned the merits of prolonging life, citing the fact that "up to half of the medical expenses incurred in the average American's life are incurred during the last six months of life". and noting the advantages of "dignity of dying in comfort" in a home setting. Carson advocated for a partially-government run plan, writing that on <a href="/wiki/End-of-life_care" title="End-of-life care">end-of-life care</a>: "Decisions on who should be treated and who should not be treated would clearly require some national guidelines."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fulltext_269-0"><a href="#cite_note-fulltext-269">[269]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fulltext_269-1"><a href="#cite_note-fulltext-269">[269]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-americanthinker.com_270-0"><a href="#cite_note-americanthinker.com-270">[270]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-271"><a href="#cite_note-271">[271]</a></sup> In January 2015, Carson stated that his views have evolved since 1992.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-272"><a href="#cite_note-272">[272]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-273"><a href="#cite_note-273">[273]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="History_of_ancient_Egypt">History of ancient Egypt</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ben_Carson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: History of ancient Egypt">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In a 1998 commencement speech at <a href="/wiki/Andrews_University" title="Andrews University">Andrews University</a>, Carson publicly expressed the view that the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pyramids_of_Giza" title="Pyramids of Giza">Pyramids of Giza</a> were not tombs, but grain silos built by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Joseph_(son_of_Jacob)" title="Joseph (son of Jacob)">Joseph, the Biblical son of Jacob</a>, in preparation for the famine depicted in the <a href="/wiki/Book_of_Genesis" title="Book of Genesis">Book of Genesis</a>. He added that "various scientists" say <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ancient_astronaut_hypothesis" title="Ancient astronaut hypothesis">ancient aliens</a> could have designed the structures, but to Carson, "it doesn't require an alien being when God is with you".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-274"><a href="#cite_note-274">[274]</a></sup> Popular in medieval Europe, the belief that Joseph had the pyramids <a href="/wiki/Joseph%27s_Granaries" title="Joseph's Granaries">built as granaries</a> was perpetuated by, among others, <a href="/wiki/Gregory_of_Tours" title="Gregory of Tours">Gregory of Tours</a> in the sixth century,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-275"><a href="#cite_note-275">[275]</a></sup> an Irish monk in the ninth century named Bernard,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-276"><a href="#cite_note-276">[276]</a></sup> a mosaic in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Mark%27s_Basilica" title="St. Mark's Basilica">St. Mark's Basilica</a> dating from the twelfth,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-277"><a href="#cite_note-277">[277]</a></sup> and the travelogue attributed to <a href="/wiki/John_Mandeville" title="John Mandeville">John Mandeville</a> in the fourteenth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-278"><a href="#cite_note-278">[278]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2015, Carson reiterated his views on the Egyptian pyramids. Archaeologists reject the notion that the pyramids were used to store grain, noting that the pyramids were not hollow, ancient Egyptian granaries have been well-studied, there is evidence of burials inside the pyramids, and the ancient Egyptians left funerary instructions inside them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Killgrove_279-0"><a href="#cite_note-Killgrove-279">[279]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-280"><a href="#cite_note-280">[280]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-281"><a href="#cite_note-281">[281]</a></sup> Additionally, the Bible states that Joseph's grain was kept in cities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ISlosers_162-1"><a href="#cite_note-ISlosers-162">[162]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Immigration">Immigration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ben_Carson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Immigration">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the <i><a href="/wiki/The_Washington_Times" title="The Washington Times">Washington Times</a></i>, Carson wrote: "Once illegals have legal status, it will be difficult to deny them any of the multitudinous entitlements that are freely distributed throughout our society." Carson believes that illegal immigrants should be able to register as guest workers and have a pathway to apply for permanent resident status.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-auto_219-1"><a href="#cite_note-auto-219">[219]</a></sup></p>
<p>In August 2015, Carson suggesting using <a href="/wiki/Unmanned_aerial_vehicle" title="Unmanned aerial vehicle">drones</a> to secure the U.S.-Mexico border. Carson said he did not favor "killing people" with drones, but favored using drones for surveillance and strikes to eliminate "the caves that are utilized to hide people" illegally entering the U.S. from Mexico.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-282"><a href="#cite_note-282">[282]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-283"><a href="#cite_note-283">[283]</a></sup></p>
<p>In September 2015, Carson said that due to the difficulty in deporting illegal immigrants, he would instead prioritize sealing the <a href="/wiki/Borders_of_the_United_States" title="Borders of the United States">borders of the United States</a>, which "in the Carson administration that would be done in the first year". He also said that "you have to also turn off the spigot that dispenses the goodies so that people don't have any incentive to come here".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-284"><a href="#cite_note-284">[284]</a></sup></p>
<p>In November 2015, Carson twice likened <a href="/wiki/Refugees_of_the_Syrian_Civil_War" title="Refugees of the Syrian Civil War">Syrian refugees</a> to "rabid dogs" and suggested that they posed a risk to American society.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-285"><a href="#cite_note-285">[285]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-286"><a href="#cite_note-286">[286]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Marijuana_and_drug_policy">Marijuana and drug policy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ben_Carson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Marijuana and drug policy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2014, Carson said that "I think <a href="/wiki/Medical_cannabis" title="Medical cannabis">medical use of marijuana</a> in compassionate cases certainly has been proven to be useful" but said that he opposed legalization of recreational <a href="/wiki/Cannabis_(drug)" title="Cannabis (drug)">marijuana</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MJ_287-0"><a href="#cite_note-MJ-287">[287]</a></sup> Carson believes marijuana is a <a href="/wiki/Gateway_drug_theory" title="Gateway drug theory">gateway drug</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MJ_287-1"><a href="#cite_note-MJ-287">[287]</a></sup> On the <a href="/wiki/Legality_of_cannabis_by_U.S._jurisdiction" title="Legality of cannabis by U.S. jurisdiction">legalization of recreational marijuana in Colorado</a>, Carson said "I don't think this is something that we really want for our society. You know, we're gradually just removing all the barriers to hedonistic activity and you know, it's just, we're changing so rapidly to a different type of society and nobody is getting a chance to discuss it because, you know, it's taboo."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MJ_287-2"><a href="#cite_note-MJ-287">[287]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-288"><a href="#cite_note-288">[288]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-289"><a href="#cite_note-289">[289]</a></sup></p>
<p>In an appearance on <a href="/wiki/Glenn_Beck" title="Glenn Beck">Glenn Beck</a>'s show, Carson said he would "intensify" the <a href="/wiki/War_on_Drugs" title="War on Drugs">War on Drugs</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-290"><a href="#cite_note-290">[290]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Marriage_and_LGBT_issues">Marriage and LGBT issues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ben_Carson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Marriage and LGBT issues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In March 2013, Carson described his views about <a href="/wiki/Same-sex_marriage_in_the_United_States" title="Same-sex marriage in the United States">same-sex marriage</a> on <i><a href="/wiki/Hannity" title="Hannity">Hannity</a></i>, saying: "Marriage is between a man and a woman. No group, be they gays, be they <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NAMBLA" title="NAMBLA">NAMBLA</a>, be they people who believe in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bestiality" title="Bestiality">bestiality</a>, it doesn't matter what they are. They don't get to change the definition."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-politico-remark_291-0"><a href="#cite_note-politico-remark-291">[291]</a></sup> The comments caused controversy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GayPrisonComment_292-0"><a href="#cite_note-GayPrisonComment-292">[292]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/GLAAD" title="GLAAD">GLAAD</a> criticized Carson for having "equated gays" with those from the North American Man/Boy Love Association and supporters of bestiality.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-293"><a href="#cite_note-293">[293]</a></sup> A number of students at the <a href="/wiki/Johns_Hopkins_School_of_Medicine" title="Johns Hopkins School of Medicine">Johns Hopkins School of Medicine</a>, "enraged by Carson's comparison of homosexuality with bestiality and pedophilia," called upon Carson to withdraw as a commencement speaker. Carson withdrew as speaker and apologized for his remarks,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-294"><a href="#cite_note-294">[294]</a></sup> saying that he was not equating those groups. He said:</p>
<blockquote>
<p>You know, as a Christian... I have a duty to love all people and that includes people who have other sexual orientations, and I certainly do, and never had any intention of offending anyone. What I was basically saying, and if anybody was offended, I apologize to you. But what I was basically saying is that there is no group. I wasn’t equating those things. I don’t think they’re equal. Just, you know, if you ask me for apple and I give you an orange you would say, well that's not an orange. And then I say, that's a banana, that's not an apple either. And there's a peach, that's not an apple, either. But it doesn’t mean that I’m equating the banana and the orange and the peach. And in the same way I’m not equating those things.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-295"><a href="#cite_note-295">[295]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>Carson further said "the examples were not the best choice of words" and that the <a href="/wiki/Bible" title="Bible">Bible</a> "says we have an obligation to love our fellow man as ourselves, and I love everybody the same—all homosexuals."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sun-withdraw_296-0"><a href="#cite_note-sun-withdraw-296">[296]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-post-withdraw_297-0"><a href="#cite_note-post-withdraw-297">[297]</a></sup> According to Carson, "I was trying to say that as far as marriage was concerned, it has traditionally been between a man and a woman and no one should be able to change that."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-insider_298-0"><a href="#cite_note-insider-298">[298]</a></sup> Carson continued to clarify his comments in later years: "That point was if you change the definition of marriage for one group, you’ll have to change it for the next group and the next group", which was characterized as a <a href="/wiki/Slippery_slope" title="Slippery slope">slippery slope</a> argument by <i><a href="/wiki/The_Washington_Post" title="The Washington Post">The Washington Post</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-299"><a href="#cite_note-299">[299]</a></sup></p>
<p>In a 2015 <a href="/wiki/Facebook" title="Facebook">Facebook</a> post, Carson wrote that he supports <a href="/wiki/Civil_union" title="Civil union">civil unions</a> for gay couples and he has "for many years".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-300"><a href="#cite_note-300">[300]</a></sup> Carson, while on the boards for <a href="/wiki/Costco" title="Costco">Costco</a> and food manufacturer <a href="/wiki/Kellogg%27s" title="Kellogg's">Kellogg's</a>, supported initiatives for employment non-discrimination, health insurance for domestic partners, and diversity training.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-301"><a href="#cite_note-301">[301]</a></sup></p>
<p>Later in 2015, reacting to an ordinance in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Houston,_Texas" title="Houston, Texas">Houston, Texas</a> that would have permitted those who are <a href="/wiki/Transgender" title="Transgender">transgender</a> to enter a bathroom designated for the gender with which they identify, Carson proposed the idea of transgender bathrooms, saying: "It is not fair for them to make everybody else uncomfortable. ... I think everybody has equal rights, but I'm not sure that anybody should have extra rights – extra rights when it comes to redefining everything for everybody else and imposing your view on everybody else."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-302"><a href="#cite_note-302">[302]</a></sup></p>
<p>In a March 2015 interview with <a href="/wiki/Chris_Cuomo" title="Chris Cuomo">Chris Cuomo</a>, Carson stated he believes homosexuality is a choice, saying: "a lot of people go into <a href="/wiki/Prison_sexuality" title="Prison sexuality">prison straight</a>, and when they come out, they're gay".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-303"><a href="#cite_note-303">[303]</a></sup> Later, in a <a href="/wiki/Facebook" title="Facebook">Facebook</a> post, Carson wrote that he "realized that my choice of language does not reflect fully my heart on gay issues. I do not pretend to know how every individual came to their sexual orientation. I regret that my words to express that concept were hurtful and divisive. For that I apologize unreservedly to all that were offended."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-304"><a href="#cite_note-304">[304]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-305"><a href="#cite_note-305">[305]</a></sup></p>
<p>In October 2014, the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Poverty_Law_Center" title="Southern Poverty Law Center">Southern Poverty Law Center</a> (SPLC) added Carson to its "anti-gay extremist" list, citing Carson's "linking gays with pedophiles" and other comments;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wong_306-0"><a href="#cite_note-Wong-306">[306]</a></sup> in February 2015, the SPLC removed Carson's name from its list and apologized to him.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-307"><a href="#cite_note-307">[307]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-308"><a href="#cite_note-308">[308]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-309"><a href="#cite_note-309">[309]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-310"><a href="#cite_note-310">[310]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_affairs_and_defense">Foreign affairs and defense</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ben_Carson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Foreign affairs and defense">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2015, Carson's "main national security adviser" was <a href="/wiki/Robert_F._Dees" title="Robert F. Dees">Robert F. Dees</a>, a retired Army major general who, like Carson, argues that national security is linked to spiritual values. Dees wrote in his book <i>Resilient Nations</i> (2014) that the greatest threat to America was not terrorism, China, or Russia but rather the decline of its "spiritual infrastructure". Dees writes:</p>
<blockquote>
<p><i>At the height of Roman decadence, good became evil and evil became good... One can rightly argue that the United States is frightfully close to a similar fate. Prayerfully, it is not too late.</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-311"><a href="#cite_note-311">[311]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>In several interviews, Carson has endorsed the views of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Political_theorist" title="Political theorist">political theorist</a> <a href="/wiki/W._Cleon_Skousen" title="W. Cleon Skousen">W. Cleon Skousen</a>, an author popular among <a href="/wiki/Tea_Party_movement" title="Tea Party movement">Tea Party</a> supporters, recommending Skousen's book <i><a href="/wiki/The_Naked_Communist" title="The Naked Communist">The Naked Communist</a></i> (1958).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kilgore_312-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kilgore-312">[312]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CornSkousen_313-0"><a href="#cite_note-CornSkousen-313">[313]</a></sup> In a July 2014 interview, Carson cited Skousen and suggested that nefarious Marxist forces were plotting to use the mainstream media to undermine the United States, saying: "There was a guy who was a former CIA agent by the name of Cleon Skousen who wrote a book in 1958 called <i>The Naked Communist</i>, and it laid out the whole agenda. You would think by reading it that it was written last year—showing what they're trying to do to American families, what they're trying to do to our Judeo-Christian faith, what they're doing to morality."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kilgore_312-1"><a href="#cite_note-Kilgore-312">[312]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CornSkousen_313-1"><a href="#cite_note-CornSkousen-313">[313]</a></sup> An endorsement from Carson appears on the front cover of the most recent edition of Skousen's book.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kilgore_312-2"><a href="#cite_note-Kilgore-312">[312]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CornSkousen_313-2"><a href="#cite_note-CornSkousen-313">[313]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Peter_Wehner" title="Peter Wehner">Peter Wehner</a>, a senior fellow at the <a href="/wiki/Ethics_and_Public_Policy_Center" title="Ethics and Public Policy Center">Ethics and Public Policy Center</a> who served in the last three Republican administrations, said that Carson views Skousen's work as "an interpretive key to America today."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-314"><a href="#cite_note-314">[314]</a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Syria">Syria</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ben_Carson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Syria">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Carson has expressed a number of often contradictory positions on the role of the United States in the <a href="/wiki/Syrian_Civil_War" title="Syrian Civil War">Syrian Civil War</a>. Carson initially opposed the Obama administration's <a href="/wiki/Authorization_for_the_Use_of_Military_Force_Against_the_Government_of_Syria_to_Respond_to_Use_of_Chemical_Weapons" title="Authorization for the Use of Military Force Against the Government of Syria to Respond to Use of Chemical Weapons">proposed military intervention in Syria</a> in September 2013, claiming that the rebels it would be in support of posed a national security threat to the United States and Israel, and disputing the allegation that the Syrian government was responsible for the use of chemical weapons.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-315"><a href="#cite_note-315">[315]</a></sup></p>
<p>By September 2015, Carson had changed his position on the <a href="/wiki/Bashar_al-Assad" title="Bashar al-Assad">Assad</a> regime, calling for forcing <a href="/wiki/Islamic_State_of_Iraq_and_the_Levant" title="Islamic State of Iraq and the Levant">ISIL</a> out of Iraq in order to allow the group to focus on overthrowing the Assad regime, whilst continuing to advocate non-intervention in Syria.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-316"><a href="#cite_note-316">[316]</a></sup> Carson then staked out a more aggressive position in October 2015, advocating for the imposition of a no-fly zone along Syria's northern border with Turkey and continued military and intelligence support for anti-Assad rebels as a means of countering Russian influence in the region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-317"><a href="#cite_note-317">[317]</a></sup></p>
<p>In November 2015, Carson once again opposed U.S. assistance to Syrian rebels, instead supporting a political solution in Syria, culminating in a coalition government that would include Assad. He justified his new position by criticizing the United States' support for rebels in the <a href="/wiki/Libyan_Civil_War_(2011)" title="Libyan Civil War (2011)">first Libyan Civil War</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-318"><a href="#cite_note-318">[318]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religious_freedom_and_separation_of_church_and_state">Religious freedom and separation of church and state</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ben_Carson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Religious freedom and separation of church and state">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In a 2014 op-ed article, Carson argued that the <a href="/wiki/First_Amendment_to_the_United_States_Constitution" title="First Amendment to the United States Constitution">First Amendment</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Establishment_Clause" title="Establishment Clause">Establishment Clause</a> has been "reinterpreted" by progressives away from its original intent, writing that "our Judeo-Christian values have taken a big hit in recent years" although "we have not yet reached the point of a totally godless government."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-319"><a href="#cite_note-319">[319]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-320"><a href="#cite_note-320">[320]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-321"><a href="#cite_note-321">[321]</a></sup> He said in May 2015: "To try to impose one's religious beliefs on someone else is absolutely what we should not be doing. That goes in both directions."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Banks_322-0"><a href="#cite_note-Banks-322">[322]</a></sup></p>
<p>During a September 2015 <i><a href="/wiki/Meet_the_Press" title="Meet the Press">Meet the Press</a></i> interview, in response to <a href="/wiki/Chuck_Todd" title="Chuck Todd">Chuck Todd</a>'s question "Should a President's faith matter [to voters]?," Carson said that if a faith is "inconsistent with the values and principles of America, then of course it should matter."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MTPfaith_323-0"><a href="#cite_note-MTPfaith-323">[323]</a></sup> Todd continued with, "So do you believe that Islam is consistent with the constitution?" to which Carson said, "No, I don't, I do not [believe so]. I would not advocate that we put a Muslim in charge of this nation. I absolutely would not agree with that."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MTPfaith_323-1"><a href="#cite_note-MTPfaith-323">[323]</a></sup> Carson maintained that sharia (Islamic law) is "something that is against the rights of women, against the rights of gays, subjugates other religions, and a host of things that are not compatible with our Constitution."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-weekpower_324-0"><a href="#cite_note-weekpower-324">[324]</a></sup> In a subsequent interview, Carson said that "anybody, doesn't matter what their religious background, if they accept American values and principles and are willing to subjugate their religious beliefs to our Constitution. I have no problem with them."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-weekpower_324-1"><a href="#cite_note-weekpower-324">[324]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards_and_honors">Awards and honors</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ben_Carson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Awards and honors">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:200px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ben_Carson_(cropped).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="202" data-file-width="198" height="202" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/14/Ben_Carson_%28cropped%29.jpg" width="198"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ben_Carson_(cropped).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Carson at the <a href="/wiki/White_House" title="White House">White House</a> in 2008 for the <a href="/wiki/Presidential_Medal_of_Freedom" title="Presidential Medal of Freedom">Presidential Medal of Freedom</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Carson is a member of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/American_Academy_of_Achievement" title="American Academy of Achievement">American Academy of Achievement</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-325"><a href="#cite_note-325">[325]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Omega_Alpha" title="Alpha Omega Alpha">Alpha Omega Alpha</a> Honor Medical Society,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-326"><a href="#cite_note-326">[326]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Horatio_Alger_Association_of_Distinguished_Americans" title="Horatio Alger Association of Distinguished Americans">Horatio Alger Association of Distinguished Americans</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-327"><a href="#cite_note-327">[327]</a></sup> Carson has been awarded 38 honorary doctorate degrees and dozens of national merit citations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-328"><a href="#cite_note-328">[328]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Detroit_Public_Schools" title="Detroit Public Schools">Detroit Public Schools</a> opened the Dr. Benjamin Carson High School of Science and Medicine<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-329"><a href="#cite_note-329">[329]</a></sup> for students interested in pursuing healthcare careers. The school is partnering with <a href="/wiki/Detroit_Receiving_Hospital" title="Detroit Receiving Hospital">Detroit Receiving Hospital</a> and <a href="/wiki/Michigan_State_University" title="Michigan State University">Michigan State University</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-330"><a href="#cite_note-330">[330]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li>In 2000, he received the Award for Greatest Public Service Benefiting the Disadvantaged, an award given out annually by <a href="/wiki/Jefferson_Awards_for_Public_Service" title="Jefferson Awards for Public Service">Jefferson Awards</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-331"><a href="#cite_note-331">[331]</a></sup></li>
<li>In 2001, he was elected by the <a href="/wiki/Library_of_Congress" title="Library of Congress">Library of Congress</a> on the occasion of its 200th anniversary to be one of the 89 who earned the designation <a href="/wiki/Library_of_Congress_Living_Legend" title="Library of Congress Living Legend">Library of Congress Living Legend</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-332"><a href="#cite_note-332">[332]</a></sup></li>
<li>In 2004, he was appointed to serve on <a href="/wiki/The_President%27s_Council_on_Bioethics" title="The President's Council on Bioethics">The President's Council on Bioethics</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-333"><a href="#cite_note-333">[333]</a></sup></li>
<li>In 2005, Carson was awarded the <a href="/wiki/William_E._Simon_Prize_for_Philanthropic_Leadership" title="William E. Simon Prize for Philanthropic Leadership">William E. Simon Prize for Philanthropic Leadership</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-334"><a href="#cite_note-334">[334]</a></sup></li>
<li>In 2006, he received the <a href="/wiki/Spingarn_Medal" title="Spingarn Medal">Spingarn Medal</a> from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NAACP" title="NAACP">NAACP</a>, their highest honor for outstanding achievement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-335"><a href="#cite_note-335">[335]</a></sup></li>
<li>In 2008, the <a href="/wiki/White_House" title="White House">White House</a> awarded Carson the <a href="/wiki/Presidential_Medal_of_Freedom" title="Presidential Medal of Freedom">Presidential Medal of Freedom</a>, the nation's highest civilian honor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-336"><a href="#cite_note-336">[336]</a></sup></li>
<li>In 2008, <a href="/wiki/Ford%27s_Theatre" title="Ford's Theatre">Ford's Theatre</a> Society awarded Carson the Ford's Theatre Lincoln Medal, for exemplifying the qualities embodied by President Abraham Lincoln—including courage, integrity, tolerance, equality, and creative expression—through superior achievements.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-337"><a href="#cite_note-337">[337]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-338"><a href="#cite_note-338">[338]</a></sup></li>
<li>In 2008, <a href="/wiki/U.S._News_%26_World_Report" title="U.S. News &amp; World Report">U.S. News &amp; World Report</a> named Carson as one of "America's Best Leaders".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-339"><a href="#cite_note-339">[339]</a></sup></li>
<li>In 2010, he was elected into the <a href="/wiki/National_Academy_of_Sciences" title="National Academy of Sciences">National Academy of Sciences</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Institute_of_Medicine" title="Institute of Medicine">Institute of Medicine</a>, considered one of the highest honors in the fields of health and medicine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-340"><a href="#cite_note-340">[340]</a></sup></li>
<li>In 2012, Carson was the Influential Marylander Award recipient from <i><a href="/wiki/Daily_Record_(Maryland)" title="Daily Record (Maryland)">The Daily Record</a></i>, Baltimore's legal and business newspaper.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-341"><a href="#cite_note-341">[341]</a></sup></li>
<li>In 2014, a poll of Americans conducted by <a href="/wiki/Gallup_(company)" title="Gallup (company)">Gallup</a> ranked Carson sixth on a list of the <a href="/wiki/Gallup%27s_most_admired_man_and_woman_poll" title="Gallup's most admired man and woman poll">most admired persons</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-342"><a href="#cite_note-342">[342]</a></sup></li>
<li>He is an <a href="/wiki/Emeritus" title="Emeritus">emeritus</a> <a href="/wiki/Fellow" title="Fellow">fellow</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Yale_Corporation" title="Yale Corporation">Yale Corporation</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-343"><a href="#cite_note-343">[343]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Books_by_Carson">Books by Carson</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ben_Carson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Books by Carson">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Biographical_works_about_Carson">Biographical works about Carson</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ben_Carson&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Biographical works about Carson">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Gifted_Hands:_The_Ben_Carson_Story" title="Gifted Hands: The Ben Carson Story">Gifted Hands: The Ben Carson Story</a></i> (February 7, 2009), a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Television_movie" title="Television movie">television movie</a> with the same title as Carson's first book premiered on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Turner_Network_Television" title="Turner Network Television">TNT</a> with Academy Award winner <a href="/wiki/Cuba_Gooding_Jr." title="Cuba Gooding Jr.">Cuba Gooding Jr.</a> in the lead role and <a href="/wiki/Kimberly_Elise" title="Kimberly Elise">Kimberly Elise</a> portraying his mother.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-344"><a href="#cite_note-344">[344]</a></sup></li>
<li><i>A Doctor in the House: My Life with Ben Carson</i> (January 5, 2016), a book by <a href="/wiki/Candy_Carson" title="Candy Carson">Candy Carson</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-345"><a href="#cite_note-345">[345]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
